  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f9f7fb4f-3a7e-4bec-a587-fe895dd03883'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Und der Tatsache, dass es einige Menschen gibt, die noch eine Rechnung mit ihr offen haben – sowohl tagsüber als auch nachts …</span>

<div id="review_1578746013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578746013" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578746013?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790796" href="/book/show/25858039-dream-on">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578746013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10249189373483950875">***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/03/review-dream-on-by-kerstin-gier.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Dream On by Kerstin Gier<br/>Book Two of the Silver Trilogy<br/>Publisher: Henry Holt and Co. (BYR) <br/>Publication Date: May 3, 2016<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Things seem to be going well for Liv Silver: she's adjusting to her new home (and her new family) in London; she has a burgeoning romance with Henry Harper, one of the cutest boys in school; and the girl who's been turning her dreams into nightmares, Anabel, is</span>
  <span id="freeText10249189373483950875" style="display:none">***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/03/review-dream-on-by-kerstin-gier.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Dream On by Kerstin Gier<br />Book Two of the Silver Trilogy<br />Publisher: Henry Holt and Co. (BYR) <br />Publication Date: May 3, 2016<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Things seem to be going well for Liv Silver: she's adjusting to her new home (and her new family) in London; she has a burgeoning romance with Henry Harper, one of the cutest boys in school; and the girl who's been turning her dreams into nightmares, Anabel, is now locked up. But serenity doesn't last for long.<br /><br />It seems that Liv's troubles are far from over--in fact, suddenly they're piling up. School gossip blogger Secrecy knows all of Liv's most intimate secrets, Henry might be hiding something from her, and at night Liv senses a dark presence following her through the corridors of the dream world. Does someone have a score to settle with Liv?<br /><br />Romance, adventure, and danger abound in Dream On, the second book in the Silver trilogy.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />What an excellent sequel! There were so many things about this book that really worked for me. This book is classic Kerstin Gier, with humor and a few awkward situations, realistic teenage speech and actions, and a hilarious and yet deceptively strong and capable heroine. Also swoony boys (and NOT in a triangle/square/pyramid "swoony boys" way). This book was a really great sequel, and an lovely addition to the series, and I can't wait to read book three!<br /><br />Liv Silver doesn't dislike her life so much; she's adjusted to living with her mother's boyfriend and his twin children, along with her, her sister, and au pair. Florence (one twin) is awful, but Grayson (the other twin) is actually a nice person, a fantastic brother that Liv never had. And Liv has been enjoying her time with Henry, the boy she adores and has been dating for over two months. And the mess with Anabel from book one is over - or is it? Someone is haunting Liv's dreams, and it's not just Liv's dreams - but Mia's too. And someone's been leaking personal information of Liv's to Secrecy, the school's blogging gossip. And what's more, Henry has been even more secretive than usual. Does it have to do with the dream world? Can Liv seek out the danger before someone gets hurt?<br /><br />I love Liv! She's funny and adorable and sweet - so sweet - and she likes to talk. She's one of those people that talks in a stream-of-consciousness kind of way, and it's hilarious. She's honest and kind and protective of her sister, her au pair, her boyfriend. I like how she seems somewhat absent-minded at times, but she's sharp as a tack. There are so many funny scenes, and also several times when I experienced some second-hand embarrassment. Ha!<br /><br />Henry is her boyfriend, and he's a pretty important character in both this book and Dream a Little Dream. Henry is really good at dream weaving/walking (however you want to call it), and he and Liv meet in the dream world often. Henry is devoted to Liv, and cares about her a great deal. He's affectionate and kind, and also protective. Did I mention that he's pretty swoony? I like him a lot, secrets and all. He has many secrets though, and it drives Liv crazy that it seems like everyone knows more about Henry than she does. I don't blame her for getting irritated about his secrets - they are secrets that affect her. <br /><br />I like the pair together. In this sequel novel, as one would expect, there are some conflicts with their relationship. Most of the conflicts have to do with Henry's secrets and Liv's doubts. I like that there are insecurities that one would find in any budding relationship, and there are also conflicts directly related to the paranormal dream aspect of the book. I like Liv and Henry together. There are plenty of swoony moments in this book, but also some heavy and heartbreaking moments. But the romance overall is good, and there is no love triangle. Also, the ending of the book makes up for some of the conflicts during the book.<br /><br />The conflicts that have nothing to do with the romance are troubling, and the climax climbs steadily until we reach the great reveal of what is happening. And even then, not everything is revealed. I like that the larger conflict of the overall plot of the book isn't a save-the-world-or-everyone-dies kind of conflict. It's serious and dangerous and crazy, but not on a world scale, which I found refreshing. And the high school gossip is not nearly as bad as the synopsis makes it out to be - it barely bothered me (and Liv, and everyone else)!<br /><br />I like how close Liv and Grayson become! Being stepsiblings forced to live together wasn't easy in Dream a Little Dream, and so I really liked seeing them get closer. Grayson looks out for Liv on more than one occasion, like a good big brother. Their relationship is purely platonic and sibling-esque!<br /><br />I've mentioned the characters, relationships, romance, plot, overall plot... I think I've covered it all! I really liked this book, and the ending is not a cruel cliffhanger like most sequels of trilogies are. I repeat: no cliffhanger! I mean, the story is definitely not resolved, and I am dying to read book three, but there is no cliffhanger!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />I'm still a tiny bit confused as to what exactly Henry was doing in his dream world (think mermaid scene), but I think this will be better explained in book three. I was hoping we'd get a more solid answer about this in particular, but I think it's one of several things that we'll know more about, in book three! Gier always does a good job of answering questions and wrapping up series.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />I love this series and highly recommend it! I know there were a number of people that didn't enjoy Dream a Little Dream, but I am enjoying this series. Gier's books are so lighthearted and fun, and realistic and relate-able. If you like paranormal books about dreams (the dream door concept is new!), this is definitely a series to try!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4 stars. More, please! I don't know how Gier does it, but you can tell her stories and writing are different from most YA stories and writing styles. I loved her Ruby Red trilogy, and I am hooked on this Silver trilogy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10249189373483950875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790796" href="/book/show/25858039-dream-on">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=annoying-tropes">annoying-tropes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=dreams">dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=eyeroll-moments">eyeroll-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013012334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14847601994295450784">I really, really want to love this series, as I am a HUGE fan of Kerstin Gier’s other work. However, this just got a bit too…cliché YA. <b>It could be sweet at times, but it lacked the originality and charms from her other series.</b><br/><br/>I was feeling the romance in the 1st book, but nope, I’m done here. Henry was just bringing too much of the cliché romance from other YAs I’ve read. <b>Too much secrecy, bad communication, and nonsensical angst.</b><br/><br/><b>In general, most of the females who were present in this book suc</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14847601994295450784" style="display:none">I really, really want to love this series, as I am a HUGE fan of Kerstin Gier’s other work. However, this just got a bit too…cliché YA. <b>It could be sweet at times, but it lacked the originality and charms from her other series.</b><br /><br />I was feeling the romance in the 1st book, but nope, I’m done here. Henry was just bringing too much of the cliché romance from other YAs I’ve read. <b>Too much secrecy, bad communication, and nonsensical angst.</b><br /><br /><b>In general, most of the females who were present in this book sucked:</b> 3 bitches who picked on the protagonist for no good reason, 1 love-crazed, superficial girl who was sorta Liv’s best friend, but heck Liv didn’t even seem to like her most of the times, 1 gold-digger, 1 murderous psychopath (literally). I was done with all of their shit. <br /><br /><b>The “dream-traveling” plot was still an interesting idea like in the first book, but I think this one lacked direction.</b> I felt like it was a fun concept, but I was bored at times. I think this book was more focused on Liv’s life at home and at school than the dream plot. I would usually be OK with that, but a lot of the stuff she was dealing with at home and at school weren’t fun to read about. Not terrible, not scarring – just unpleasant (except for the stuff about Lottie and Mia). <b>Also, there was perhaps too much attention on the school gossip website (Gossip Girl style).</b> Also-also, the villain of this book had such a childish, stupid reason to enact revenge. I mean I suppose a lot of villains do evil things for no good reason, but I’m just like reallyyyy??? Furthermore, I saw the mystery of who the villain was a mile away because I mean.. this book didn’t have many characters, so it wasn’t hard to guess.<br /><br />Anyway, ranting aside - there were some sweet moments in this book. The only good, pure characters would be Lottie, Liv’s au pair, and Mia, Liv’s younger sister. In addition, Grayson, her almost stepbrother was pretty sweet at times, despite his flaws. These characters were immensely caring and good to Liv. <b>They were funny and warm and the true bright spots of this book.</b> I appreciated that.<br /><br />This book was not… the worst. It was pretty entertaining at times. However, as a whole, it was lacking. For my own preferences, I wanted some good, healthy female friendships and some good, healthy romance and some good, healthy self-love from my YA. And if not those, I would like some kickass character developments from lowly state to self-actualization in these areas. Anyway, this book had a few good moments, but it was definitely not my cup of tea. I’m giving it <b>2 stars</b>.<br /><br />I am looking forward to see how the next and LAST book would be like because who knows? Things might turn around.<br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below) </b></u><br />Is there a happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cliffhanger, but not the last book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No actual love triangle.<br />Debatable cheating – I really can’t tell. So Liv followed Henry to his visit to a girl’s dream, and that girl he was visiting was naked and flirting with him. (Liv was hiding somewhere at this time) Right when the girl was moving in on him, Liv appeared and Henry had the “guilty look.” <br /><br />Then, after all that, Henry wanted to apologize but AT THE SAME TIME, he did not want to explain himself really. Liv was giving him a chance to explain himself, but he was like “it’s complicated. You wouldn’t understand.” And I’m like what the heck, just say it! <br /><br />Anyway, it turned out that the girl was his father’s girlfriend (gross), and Henry was trying to convince her to break up with him (I think). However, very cringe that this girl was probably having sex with his dad, while lusting after the son (gross gross gross). <br /><br />My problem with this, besides the sticky situation, was the way Henry handled it. Like, hey it wasn’t that hard to explain that to your GIRLFRIEND who should know this stuff. Also, Henry said to Liv that “it’s just a dream” and that he would have done anything to complete his task while adapting to the girl’s dreams. This was implying that he would have made out with (maybe even have sex with – IDK) his father’s gross girlfriend in the dream – who was naked in this dream, mind you – if it meant achieving his goal. Just because “it’s a dream.” <br /><br />And I get the whole “it’s a dream” argument but since Henry and Liv are literally dream-travelers and can do whatever the fuck they want consciously, then it’s not right. I mean, it’s one thing to dream about something unconsciously because you can’t really help that, but no, Henry is consciously making the choice of cheating on Liv to reach his own goal. Like, seriously? Of course, at this moment, we don’t necessarily know how far he has gone or would have gone with the girl, but ugh he was so irritating, and I was done with his secrecy.<br /><br />Medium angst. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Some. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Teens and up. Talks of sex, but no actual sex.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />----------<br />I don't really believe in "second book syndrome" but OK I'm really hoping this book will make me love this series. I absolutely adore this author but I am not (yet) entirely convinced on this series.<br /><br />Also, that cover is absolutely gorgeous!❤️</span>
  <a data-text-id="14847601994295450784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

In fact, I think it was actually really well done.   <span id="freeText14768340822375245357" style="display:none">4.5 stars rounded up because I really thoroughly enjoyed this! <br /><br />This book takes place a couple months after book 1 left off and I felt that the time jump didn't impact the series in a good way. In fact, I think it was actually really well done. I felt like the character progressions where fine the way they were and that relationships didn't suffer or feel too advanced.<br /><br />Plot wise, I liked the overall theme of this one better than book 1, but I didn't like individual plot points. The Mr. Snuggles plot point was ridiculous, the love interest drama was sort of thrown in seemingly for no reason, and I felt it actually caused the strong female character to disintegrate a bit. I love her still, dearly, but I think she can be so much stronger than she was in this book for some of it. <br /><br />Overall, enjoyable. Cannot wait to finish the series, I should get the last book tomorrow from the mailman, and I cannot wait to finish off this trilogy! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9730952313443133043">I've really enjoyed al of Kerstin's books, so I was beyond eager to get my greedy hands on this one. <br/><br/>As always, I love Liv and Mia. Their relationship is filled with banter. Liv is a snark machine and being in her head is a lot of fun.   <span id="freeText9730952313443133043" style="display:none">I've really enjoyed al of Kerstin's books, so I was beyond eager to get my greedy hands on this one. <br /><br />As always, I love Liv and Mia. Their relationship is filled with banter. Liv is a snark machine and being in her head is a lot of fun. This entire cast of characters makes the story interesting. <br /><br />The downside to the second book in a trilogy is that it's sometimes seems useless. And while I did enjoy this story, I don't feel like any of it was necessary. Sure, we did find a few things out, but mostly it felt like nothing progressed plot wise. <br /><br />Regardless, I'll definitely be reading the next book. I can't wait to see how it all ends. <br /><br />**Huge thanks to Henry Holt for sending me an arc in exchange for an honest review**</span>

As well as the fact that when he first kissed Liv, it was in a dream as well, does that mean it 'didn't count in his book'? I loved the MC, the girl friendship, the plot, the side characters and how funny it was... Everything but the love interest and the romance. <br />In The Silver trilogy, I actually did find the romance cute in the first book, but here it has definitely gone into the unbearable territory for me once again. <br /><br />Who I did like just as much here (if not more) - both as a character and his friendship with the MC - was Grayson though. He is definitely my favourite fromthe whole group of boys. I also liked the MC's sister and a few other secondary characters in her family.</span>

  <span id="freeText7551020431216916382" style="display:none">3.5 stars!<br /><br />Looks like Liv has even more problems now than before. Someone or something sinister is in following her in the corridors of the dream world. Her sister is sleepwalking, and is unintentionally putting herself and Liv in danger.<br /><br />Liv and Henry were cute together, but they didn’t really do a lot of talking. I wish they would have spent more time in the real world, because nothing made sense in the dream world. It all got perplexing sometimes.<br /><br />It would be nice if there were more explanations in the next book! I still have a lot of questions.</span>

<div id="review_2466693035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466693035" />
    <a title="Sofii♡ (A Book. A Thought.)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought"><img alt="Sofii♡ (A Book. A Thought.)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599560922p2/50405799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2466693035?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofii♡ (A Book. A Thought.)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofii♡ (A Book. A Thought.)" href="/user/show/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought">Sofii♡ (A Book. A Thought.)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790796" href="/book/show/25858039-dream-on">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50405799-sofii-a-book-a-thought?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2466693035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7528431458084694462"><br/><u>Well, this is probably one of the biggest disappointments I've had this year.</u> I think the idea of creating a story based on dreams, mysterious and terrifying things is sensational, in fact, that's what caught me in the first book. But sadly, <i>I feel that the author has decided to take another path with her sequel and take the whole plot to a completely different plane, even the characters seemed strange to me. <b>Maybe this change of the plot could be something that you enjoy, but wasn't for me.</b></i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533845327ra/26103012.gif' width='500' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>2.5/</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7528431458084694462" style="display:none"><br><u>Well, this is probably one of the biggest disappointments I've had this year.</u> I think the idea of creating a story based on dreams, mysterious and terrifying things is sensational, in fact, that's what caught me in the first book. But sadly, <i>I feel that the author has decided to take another path with her sequel and take the whole plot to a completely different plane, even the characters seemed strange to me. <b>Maybe this change of the plot could be something that you enjoy, but wasn't for me.</b></i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533845327ra/26103012.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br><br><i>You can find this one and more of my reviews on my blog <a href="https://abookathoughtblog.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Book. A Thought.</a></i><br><br><br><b>
  <i>I can't tell you what this book is about exactly because in case you want to read the trilogy it would be spoilers, but I can summarize what the first book is about and the story in general. These books follow the character of Liv Silver, many strange things have started to happen to her since she came to live, along with her sister, to England with her mother and stepfather, things that are very difficult to explain to a scientific mind like Liv's. She begins to have these very strange dreams, which feel very real and she sees in them a group of boys, which end up being the popular kids from the school where she attends to, but they suddenly seem to know everything about her, and how is that possible?!, unless they really are getting into her dreams.</i>
</b><br><br><br>So that it's kind of how the first book started, which I enjoyed a lot, I have a review about it as well if you want to check it out, but yes, <i>I was very excited because it was a light and fun reading, the idea is brillant, you can do a lot of incredible things with dreams. </i><u>But this is where Dream On comes ... where I was expecting something similar to the first book but to my surprise I found something completely different ...</u><br><br><b>Even when I knew that the characters wouldn't be incredible <i>(with the exception of Greyson, he's an angel)</i>, I expected, at least, some growth in them, and not only did I not find that, but I feel as if they were not the same characters as they were in the first book</b>, <u>many of their actions are meaningless and they act in very immature ways</u>. Especially I was surprised to see <b>Liv</b> behaving this way, in fact something happens with her new grandmother, and she takes revenge against this woman doing something abolutely meaningless and out of place that lasts like thousands of pages, I mean, doesn't even contribute or has something to do with the main plot, that was very uncomfortable to read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533845692ra/26103019.gif" width="500" height="289" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There's something about the romance that becomes so toxic and weird</b>, <i>Harry's all the time keeping secrets and playing the mysterious guy, so Liv asks him for explanations and he acts like "Can I kiss you instead?", And Liv is like "Oh OK", and I was like Excuse Me??! LOL.</i> I swear I don't exaggerate, the dialogues are something like that and it was too much for me.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>Then the most important thing, and perhaps what most influenced on myself, is that it no longer focuses on the dream world as fully as it did in the first book</b>
</i>, now it's all about Secrecy, discovering her/he identity and about the gossip that she/he writes about them. And even when,I love Gossip Girl, and the types of books with this theme are fun, in this case it felt strange and it wasn't what I was looking for in the first place when I wanted to continue with this trilogy.<br><i>
  <u>This is super personal you guys, I think maybe other people could enjoy it but it took me by surprise and made me lose interest in continuing with this trilogy. In addition to this, there is a new villain and I think it was very predictable from the beginning, so I didn't really care that much</u>
</i><br><br><br><u>Leaving aside all this, I want to mention the things that I liked:</u><br><b>I love the writing style</b> of the author, I think it's easy and quick to read and because of this I'm very interested in trying her most famous trilogy, Precious Stones, especially because I think it's about time travel and that's my jam! .<br><b>I also think that the last maybe 15 or 20% of the book was pretty good</b> and I could almost see my characters again and I liked that<br><br><br><i>
  <b>I can't really say that I would recommend this book, sadly it has been a disappointment for me, even so, if you want to try the first book it's very good!, and if you decide to continue with this one the best thing is that you have your mind open to other possibilities, the plot takes another absolutely different course and this may please or not. But to be honest I really hope that if you think about reading this book, you end up enjoying it more than me</b>
</i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7528431458084694462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790796" href="/book/show/25858039-dream-on">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1517578912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10536163290821879115">2.5 stars<br/><br/>Okay, so I enjoyed Dream On. There’s something just so compulsively fun about Kerstin Gier’s books that makes me devour them even when the plot is not on point, which tbh it’s generally not. However, there were just a lot of weird things going on in Dream On that distracted me from my usual level of enjoyment.<br/><br/>First, and I think I forgot to address this in my Dream a Little Dream review, but there’s the whole Gossip Girl plot line, which seems a bit hackneyed given, you know, Gossip Girl</span>
  <span id="freeText10536163290821879115" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />Okay, so I enjoyed Dream On. There’s something just so compulsively fun about Kerstin Gier’s books that makes me devour them even when the plot is not on point, which tbh it’s generally not. However, there were just a lot of weird things going on in Dream On that distracted me from my usual level of enjoyment.<br /><br />First, and I think I forgot to address this in my Dream a Little Dream review, but there’s the whole Gossip Girl plot line, which seems a bit hackneyed given, you know, Gossip Girl. Obviously that’s going to tie in during book three, but it’s just this occasional plot device for getting drama out there right now. Mostly, it’s for making Liv doubt Henry so they can have a big blow up in Dream On. Which ugh.<br /><br />Then there’s the thing in this book where Mia and Liv destroy their future step-grandmother’s topiary in revenge for her being a monster bitch. The whole town is pissed off because they loved the topiary. Like, the anger continues for a couple hundred pages. IT IS A BUSH. LET IT GO.<br /><br />This book’s villain was kinda weak, or at least the red herring villain was. The whole Senator Tod anagram thing felt like the villain in a kid’s book, not at all sophisticated enough for a YA novel. The underlying villain of the novel is a bit better, but it still felt like a holding pattern for book three. Basically, it seems like they wanted to keep Gier doing trilogies so they shoved a third book in even though the plot didn’t really merit it.<br /><br />If you’re into Gier’s books, Dream On‘s still worth the time, I think, but it’s not her best. I’m hoping it all comes together in book three.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10536163290821879115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17634894954423220143"><b>Gossip Girl meets Inception...and it totally works</b><br/>I rarely read sequels, but I am glad I made an exception in this case. <i>Dream On</i> was even better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090.Dream_a_Little_Dream__The_Silver_Trilogy___1_' title='Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dream a Little Dream</a>. The characters and plot line were much more believable and the writing was, as ever, charming. F4 finally got some personality. I even started to like Henry! <br/>This book skirts around the smut that usually comes with Book 2 in a series (sigh, I'm talking about you, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15755296.Through_the_Zombie_Glass__White_Rabbit_Chronicles___2_' title='Through the Zombie Glass (White Rabbit Chronicles, #2) by Gena Showalter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through the Zombie Glass</a>) and provides some actual, realistic r</span>
  <span id="freeText17634894954423220143" style="display:none"><b>Gossip Girl meets Inception...and it totally works</b><br />I rarely read sequels, but I am glad I made an exception in this case. <i>Dream On</i> was even better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469090.Dream_a_Little_Dream__The_Silver_Trilogy___1_" title="Dream a Little Dream (The Silver Trilogy, #1) by Kerstin Gier" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream a Little Dream</a>. I even started to like Henry! <br />This book skirts around the smut that usually comes with Book 2 in a series (sigh, I'm talking about you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15755296.Through_the_Zombie_Glass__White_Rabbit_Chronicles___2_" title="Through the Zombie Glass (White Rabbit Chronicles, #2) by Gena Showalter" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Zombie Glass</a>) and provides some actual, realistic relationship challenges for our heroine and hero. I rather approved of where they were at at the end. It was believable. <br />The villain was a tad predictable but the plot line had just enough underlying creepiness to keep me glued to the pages wayyyyy later than I planned. <br />I can't wait to get my hands on the third book! Seriously, one of these days I'm just going to just learn German so I don't have to wait in suspense. </span>

<div id="review_1521920833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521920833" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1714237-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341336065p2/1714237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1521920833?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/1714237-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23179355-dream-on">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1714237-lauren?shelf=pub-macmillan">pub-macmillan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1714237-lauren?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1521920833&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1521920833" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7713744783745386116">3.5 stars! <br/><br/><i>Dream On</i> is the second book in the Silver Trilogy and the follow up to Dream a Little Dream. As with the first in this series, the reason I adore these books so much is because of the MC and narrator, Liv Silver. I just love her voice. It is personable, chatty and a little bit scattered at times. I find her endlessly amusing and adorable. Even when angst and crazy things are happening, I am unable to get stressed out, while being inside of her head. <br/><br/>That said, I had a few issues with </span>
  <span id="freeText7713744783745386116" style="display:none">3.5 stars! <br /><br /><i>Dream On</i> is the second book in the Silver Trilogy and the follow up to Dream a Little Dream. As with the first in this series, the reason I adore these books so much is because of the MC and narrator, Liv Silver. I just love her voice. It is personable, chatty and a little bit scattered at times. I find her endlessly amusing and adorable. Even when angst and crazy things are happening, I am unable to get stressed out, while being inside of her head. <br /><br />That said, I had a few issues with this book. First it took me quite a while to figure out what the plot of this installment was supposed to be. At least the first third of the story I was wondering where it was going. Thankfully, I was just enjoying Liv so much that it didn't matter too much to me. Second, while I think the idea of a corridor with dream doors + people's ability to visit (and even manipulate) each other's dreams, is incredibly interesting, and I've enjoyed that set-up of the story so much, I've not been tremendously convinced of the agency of the villains in this installment. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They're basically vindictive mean girls (and boy) on a power trip with the use of dreams. I mean some of the things they've attempted have been really horrible and just over the top! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Liv's romance with Henry encounters some bumps in this story, which I was expecting. He is a boy with a lot of secrets, who doesn't open up very well, and that causes some problems between him and Liv. The good thing is that we do find out more about him and their relationship was working itself out by the end of this installment. Also, they were able to work together despite the drama between them. The bad thing is that everything isn't resolved, and I want some more explanation from him about some of his behavior. I'm not at all ultimately worried about them, but I am eager for some more talking between them <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and some groveling from Henry <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />Overall, a fun middle book, but it definitely has it's bumps, and I'm not overly convinced at why these "villains" are so out to get Liv and friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7713744783745386116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1403442865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403442865" />
    <a title="Laura (midorireads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2135787-laura-midorireads"><img alt="Laura (midorireads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434158512p2/2135787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1403442865?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura (midorireads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura (midorireads)" href="/user/show/2135787-laura-midorireads">Laura (midorireads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781627790796" href="/book/show/25858039-dream-on">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1403442865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12990894477080429739">In book 2 of the Silver Trilogy, we are fresh off the the fact that Anabel has been locked up in a psychiatric hospital, and Liv now happens to be dating Henry, a very popular and very good-looking boy from school.<br/><br/><u>BUT</u>...<br/><br/>And of course there's a <b>'but'</b>...<br/><br/><b>
  <i>BUT,</i>
</b> things are slowly beginning to unravel for Liv. Her sister is doing dangerous things while sleep-walking, Henry has become uncomfortably distant, and suddenly her secrets are beginning to show up on the blog of anonymous school blogger, Se</span>
  <span id="freeText12990894477080429739" style="display:none">In book 2 of the Silver Trilogy, we are fresh off the the fact that Anabel has been locked up in a psychiatric hospital, and Liv now happens to be dating Henry, a very popular and very good-looking boy from school.<br /><br /><u>BUT</u>...<br /><br />And of course there's a <b>'but'</b>...<br /><br /><b>
  <i>BUT,</i>
</b> things are slowly beginning to unravel for Liv. Her sister is doing dangerous things while sleep-walking, Henry has become uncomfortably distant, and suddenly her secrets are beginning to show up on the blog of anonymous school blogger, Secrecy. <br />With all of these things happening to/around Liv, we can help but wonder if someone is out and get her, and if so, who could it possibly be, and why?<br /><br />So, Liv continues to be an interesting MC for me. I still love the fact that she is mostly average, but is able to control her dreams, and knows how to open doors to dreams of others. (I just can't help but enjoy the concept of being so aware in your dream, that you're able to control it to how <i>you</i> want it to go!) <br /><br />Timing-wise, the book could be slow at parts and that had me slightly bored, but then something would happen to change my mind! Like the attack of a neighborhood relic and pillar, the topiary peacock Mr. Snuggles. I loved the whole situation that surrounded said topiary, and it certainly highlighted some of humor that was in this story, and you really could tell a person's demeanor by how they reacted to the peacock's demise.<br /><br />The romance wasn't bad and since it was still in the early stages that has the couple quite infatuated with each other, though there is the usual insecurities. It's insecurity that torturers Liv, and when she realizes she doesn't really know much about Henry.<br /><br />Now, as I come to the end of my review, I wanted to say that I am really looking forward to reading the final book, and to find out who is behind Secrecy!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12990894477080429739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8201219316829339959" style="display:none">A 3 STAR read, perhaps a 3.5 if I'm feeling generous. <br /><br />I feel like this series has a lot of potential: I like the narrator; the surrounding cast of characters are quirky and individual enough to be memorable; there's an interesting plot premise and there's cute private school boys involved (Hello, Raven Boys) - but it's like being constantly stuck on the introduction to a song. You want the verse, the bridge and chorus to crescendo into something and this... never does. It just bobs along: the equivalent of listening to a flute playing when you'd booked to see the Symphonic orchestra. <br /><br />I'm intrigued enough that I'll read the third book and because I like the authors style but if you're a casual reader, I'd probably steer clear of this one.</span>

        <a title="Ahnya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahnya" href="/user/show/2121723-ahnya">Ahnya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2121723-ahnya?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2014871881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18001449129059397792">In the second installment in the Silver series, Liv Silver is still attending Frognal Academy, dating Henry, and totally obsessed with the dream world. Almost being sacrificed to a demon by Anabel and Arthur does not slow her down a bit. Liv is still entering the dream corridor every night, and is getting pretty good at changing her appearance and surroundings in the dream world. Unfortunately "Secrecy" is still targeting her and revealing all her darkest secrets to the whole school on her blog.</span>
  <span id="freeText18001449129059397792" style="display:none">In the second installment in the Silver series, Liv Silver is still attending Frognal Academy, dating Henry, and totally obsessed with the dream world. Almost being sacrificed to a demon by Anabel and Arthur does not slow her down a bit. Liv is still entering the dream corridor every night, and is getting pretty good at changing her appearance and surroundings in the dream world. Unfortunately "Secrecy" is still targeting her and revealing all her darkest secrets to the whole school on her blog. Also, it seems like someone is trying to kill her little sister. She has recently started sleep walking, and tried to jump out of a window twice. Liv suspects Anabel is trying to take revenge for thwarting her demon sacrifice, and being committed to and asylum as a result. <br /><br />I love this series! I am really liking Kerstin as a writer. She has a great wit. Again I think some things get lost in translation, but it isn't too bad. Some of the teen drama irritates me, but you expect it when reading a YA, so I overlook it. I think the concept of the story is so imaginative. It is fun to think that if I could just find my dream door, and walk through...</span>
  <a data-text-id="18001449129059397792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AtqlP3VhnutcsxQySIfIq9S8Rdr+4rOaLkb81MfreF7ProaXw5P5oySs/sidKTkbzYekW7cYCwW8aFyy0J0AAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
